The Municipal Government Agreed to Reduce the Land Transfer Tax for Land Transactions

Changed to Collecting Two Percent of the Original Tax Amount

The North-South Land Value Tax is Limited to Clearance in February

The Fahua and Pusong Districts Will Begin Collection on March 1st

Dagon News Agency Reports: Regarding the transfer tax that should be levied on land transactions in this city, the fixed amount is very large. The municipal government authorities had once reduced it to ease the burden on property owners. Since the formal collection of the city's land value tax began on December 20 last year, in order to tighten the prosperity of land, the original amount of the transfer tax has been specially reduced again. The method of conforming to the reduction standard has now been agreed upon and implemented by the Finance and Land Bureaus. The land owners in the South Shanghai and Zhabei areas are actively paying land value tax. The Fahua and Pusong districts are scheduled to start collection on March 1st. The details are as follows:

Reducing the Transfer Tax

The land transaction transfer tax is also one of the municipal tax revenues. The fixed tax amount is very large. In addition to collecting nine percent of the current price as tax, there is an additional one percent for transfer fees, one percent for special construction donations, five percent for municipal expenses, two percent for land protection stamping fees, three percent for intermediary fees, and two percent for handling fees, totaling about 20 percent of the current price. In 1931, the municipal government authorities had once exempted all the construction special donations, transfer fees, municipal expenses, handling fees, and other fees added to the transfer tax. Only the transfer tax was implemented in the city treasury, and it was also changed to eight percent at the same time. However, the form alone incurs a handling fee of one percent due to the contract procedures, totaling nine percent levied on the current price. Since the north and south districts formally started to collect the estimated land value tax on December 20 last year, in order to prosper the land, the municipal government specially ordered the Finance and Land Bureaus to discuss and decide on methods suitable for reducing the standard, based on Article 11 of the Provisional Rules for the City Land Value Tax. According to Dagon News Agency reporters, the transfer tax has been formulated by the two bureaus. For land transfer tax in the three regions of land value tax collection, two percent of the current price will be collected, which is 7.6 percent lighter than the previous tax amount, that is, compared with the transfer tax outside the land value tax area, it is also reduced by three-quarters.

Land Value Tax Enthusiasm

The land owners in South Shanghai, from Block 1 to Block 8, and in Zhabei, Blocks 1 and 2, after the valuation committee estimated the value of the land reported by the owners and determined the tax rate, were formally opened for collection by the Finance Bureau's instructions to the South Shanghai and Zhabei tax collection offices on December 20 last year. Up to now, for a month, the land owners in each block have been actively going to pay the land value tax in accordance with the assessment with the land business license and the tax payment notice. The total has reached six out of ten.

Fahua and Pusong to Begin Collection

The city land bureau is continuing to collect the land value tax in the Fahua and Pusong districts. The investigation of the Fahua district has been completed, and the Pusong district has also begun. Each block that has been investigated has notified the owners to report the land value automatically from January 11 to February 10 this year. After preliminary assessment, it will be submitted to the Land Valuation Committee for review and then sent to the Finance Bureau for joint announcement of collection. Therefore, the land value tax in the Fahua and Pusong districts has been set to be implemented on March 1st.

Japanese Espionage in the Northwest: Eurasia Aviation Corporation Ordered to Take Precautions

No New Discoveries After Previous Detention

According to the Xin Sheng News Agency, since the Japanese occupied our Northeast, they have recently instigated Puyi to declare himself emperor and are now deploying troops to spy on the west. Their ambition has been fully exposed and has not diminished at all. Since the recent unrest, there have been daily reports of Japanese agents infiltrating key areas in the Northwest to spy. Some have even disguised themselves and traveled on Eurasia Aviation Corporation planes to Gansu, and then proceeded to Xinjiang. The Xin Sheng News Agency reporter, recognizing the immense implications of this matter for national defense, visited the corporation's Secretary Zha yesterday to inquire about the situation. According to him, recently, no Japanese nationals have been discovered using the company's planes to travel to the Northwest. The only case was a Japanese national introduced by a commissioner from a certain agency, who was

inspected and detained by Chairman Zhu (Shaoliang). He has not been seen again since. Although there are rumors circulating outside, they definitely do not involve travel on this

company's planes. However, because this company is engaged in commercial operations, there have been no restrictions on the nationality of passengers. But since the previous incident of a Japanese national secretly traveling to the Northwest to take photos of the interior, the Ministry of Communications has reiterated a strict ban. Regardless of nationality, all passengers disembarking at any of the company's stations must be subject to inspection by local military and police authorities to prevent any improper actions that could harm our national defense. At the same time, passengers must provide accurate names,

addresses, and telephone numbers when purchasing tickets for verification purposes. In fact, the precautions are already extremely strict.

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company: Revised Plans for Geng款 Shipbuilding Program: Redetermining Construction Plans for Jianghai Vessels

Revised Hull Length for the "Sihai" Vessels

Orders to Commissioners in England to Re-tender Bids

Decision to Build Two of the Three "Changjiang" Vessels First

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, using the British Boxer Indemnity funds to build four ocean-going vessels and three river vessels, had already held bidding processes in both London and Shanghai. However, due to the high cost of the ocean-going vessels, which far exceeded the budget, the entire shipbuilding plan underwent significant changes. Not only was the ocean-going vessel project halted, but the river vessel construction could not proceed according to the original plan. This matter has been reported in this newspaper. Recently, the company, along with the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Board of Trustees, has repeatedly consulted with and petitioned the Ministry of Communications, exchanging letters and telegrams and holding meetings to find remedial measures. A revised plan has finally been agreed upon. The key points of the situation

are summarized below:

Negotiating Ocean-Going Vessel Costs

Since the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company appointed Wu Daming and Shi Gan to London, a bidding process was held for the "Sihai" vessels. As a result, the lowest bid for each vessel was 90,000 British pounds, which was 25,000 pounds higher than the company's budget. Each vessel would cost 400,000 yuan, and four vessels would exceed 1.6 million yuan, which would jeopardize the funding for the river vessels as well. This has been raised at several board meetings this month for discussion. After deliberation by the heads of each department, it was decided that due to the loan agreement, the vessels must be built in England and cannot be constructed at shipyards in other countries. However, the excessively high price of the vessels was deemed uneconomical. Therefore, the Ministry was consulted, and the company decided to cable Wu and Shi in London, instructing them not to sign the new vessel bids for the time being, pending further instructions.

Boxer Indemnity Board's Inquiry

The Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Board of Trustees has the right to advise on shipbuilding bids. After Wu and Shi telegraphed the total cost to the head office, the Board of Trustees also repeatedly inquired from the company whether to proceed with the construction. Liu Hongsheng believed that the bid price for the four vessels was one-quarter higher than the budget. If the vessels were constructed at this price, the three river vessels would be entirely scrapped, which would deviate significantly from the original plan. Therefore, he replied to the Board of Trustees that the cost of the four new vessels required careful consideration and that construction would proceed after a decision was made.

Re-tendering Bids

The company submitted a report to the Board of Directors and the Ministry of Communications regarding the cost of the "Sihai" vessels, requesting guidance on how to proceed. The shipbuilding department also had the bid documents sent from London reviewed by Department Heads Zhao and Zhou. After a detailed examination, it was found that the vessel length listed in the bids from England was 340 feet, which did not match the company's proposed dimensions. Therefore, the company will provide more detailed specifications for the vessel's size, tonnage, draft, etc., to Wu and Shi in England, instructing them to re-tender bids in England to ensure that they meet the budget.

Building Two River Vessels First

The remaining funds from the Boxer Indemnity, according to the original budget, would allow for an additional 140,000 pounds, which was earmarked for the construction of three Yangtze River vessels. Bids had already been invited in Shanghai, with plans for the Jiangnan Shipyard to build the hulls and the engines to be shipped from England. Now, due to the higher-than-budgeted cost of the "Sihai" vessels, the three river vessels have also been affected. The company has submitted a report to the Ministry requesting instructions on how to proceed. A reply has now been received from the Ministry, instructing that, regarding the construction of the river vessels in Shanghai, the shipyard should be contacted to build two vessels first. The engines, materials, and the four "Sihai" vessels should wait until a second round of bidding in England is held, and the prices are determined before raising funds to cover the deficit. Therefore, the company has decided to proceed with ordering two Yangtze River vessels in Shanghai first, and the Jiangnan Shipyard has sent representatives to the company to negotiate the construction procedures.

Taihu Water Conservancy Association Announces Songjiang Dredging Plan

Estimated Cost of 2.14 Million Yuan

The Taihu Lake Basin Water Conservancy Commission's proposal to request an allocation of cotton and wheat loans to dredge the Wusong River to benefit commerce and agriculture has been reported previously. The Xin Sheng News Agency has learned that the commission, based on the actual survey charts of the former Taihu Lake Water Conservancy Project Office, the former Jiangnan Water Conservancy Bureau, and the Shanghai Dredging Bureau, as well as the Construction Committee's decision to dredge the Wusong River, has released the following plan:

Construction Sections

The upstream section, from Guajingkou to Jianghe Village, is about 18 li. The width of the river in this section is more than 40 meters, and there are no overly narrow areas. However, there are silted and shallow areas in the riverbed that should be dredged to make the riverbed at least 0.85 meters lower than the Wusong River's zero mark. The downstream section, from Xugonggangkou East to Fanwangdu, is about 59 li. This section is the shallowest and narrowest. Since the Republic era, there have been long-standing desires to dredge it, but it has not been implemented. This section cannot be effectively treated without major dredging and cannot be done in stages. For the section from Fanwangdu East to the Waibaidu Bridge, the Shanghai Port Authority's estimates will be used to address areas requiring treatment.

Cutting Out Bends

The Wusong River's upstream section has a wide river and deep channel, similar to a lake. Although there are some bends, the branch ports and small rivers in between connect up and down, allowing for drainage during high tides. Therefore, there is no need to invest heavily in cutting them out. Also, between 40 and 50 meters from the entrance of Guajing, the riverbed is elevated, even above the Wusong zero mark. However, the main current has already abandoned the bend and flows through Huaxiang Port, which is 150 meters wide, and the riverbed is 1.0 to 2.0 meters lower than the Wusong zero mark. Therefore, the original river can also be left as it is. However, the Yejidun section downstream has the most bends and is the most prone to siltation. All proposed dredging plans to reroute it have been stopped due to the difficulty and expense of the project. Now, it is proposed to cut out the section from Anlangdu to Zhangjiadu at Yejidun and open a new river channel, which will be more than 2,900 meters long (refer to the opinion of the former Jiangnan Water Conservancy Bureau), 46 meters wide, an average of 5.396 feet deep, and 17.2 meters wide at the bottom, for a total of

174,000 cubic yards of compacted soil (provisionally estimated at 170,000).

Volume of Earthwork

The volume of earthwork for each section is based on cubic yards of compacted soil. The list is as follows: Guajingkou to Jianghe Village: 12,913.0 cubic yards; Xugonggang to Anlangdu: 391,494.0 cubic yards (excluding the Anlangdu to Zhangjiadu section); Zhangjiadu to Fanwangdu: 120,404.0 cubic yards; Fanwangdu to Xinzha Bridge: 122,500.0 cubic yards; Xinzha Bridge to Waibaidu Bridge: 56,220.0 cubic yards (The Shanghai Dredging Bureau has completed a portion of the project in the section from Fanwangdu to Waibaidu Bridge. This amount of earthwork should be deducted during future construction.) The total is 703,530.0 cubic yards. The earthwork for the new river channel is estimated to be 170,000 cubic yards. It is estimated that the earthwork above the water level accounts for about 54% of the total, while the earthwork below the water level accounts for about 46% of the total.

Dredging Method

The dredging project consists of two methods: manual excavation and mechanical ship excavation. However, the use of manual labor in previous projects took several months, causing transportation disruptions and harming agriculture and commerce. Furthermore, the river has a dense network of tributaries, and it is estimated that there are more than one hundred dams. Constructing dams and isolating water requires significant labor and expense. With the exception of manual excavation for the section cutting the bend at Anpai Ferry, it is appropriate to use mechanical ship excavation across the board. It can also be carried out over several years, and funding can be arranged in a relaxed manner, which is a win-win situation.

Budget

The total earthwork, excluding the project to cut the bend and straighten the river, is about 700,000 cubic yards of compacted soil, which is 1,050,000 cubic yards of wet soil. It is planned to be carried out over six years, with 170,000 cubic yards of earthwork excavated each year. Excluding repairs and other reasons for suspending work, the working time is estimated at 250 days per year, requiring 700 cubic yards of earthwork to be excavated each day. It is now planned to purchase one large dredger and two small dredgers so that the total amount of earthwork can be completed within six years. The complete budget for the dredging project after the dredging is completed and the annual budget are listed below. (1) Total cost of earthwork: 1,515,460 yuan; first year's expenses: 215,460 yuan; expenses for the second to sixth years: 260,000 yuan per year. (2) Total cost of land acquisition: 66,750 yuan; expenses for the first year: 66,750 yuan (the above amount is for the acquisition of private land for cutting the bend and widening the river). (3) Total cost of three dredgers, large and small: 310,000 yuan. (4) Total cost of two tugboats: 50,000 yuan. (5) Total cost of machine factory and equipment: 10,000 yuan. (6) Total administrative expenses for six years: 120,000 yuan. (7) Total reserve expenses: 67,790 yuan. The total is 2,140,000 yuan.

Hong Kong & Whampoa Dockyard Barge Workers on Strike

Clash Results in Multiple Injuries

After a strike at the Hong Kong & Whampoa Dockyard Towboat Company last year, another incident occurred when the company dismissed a worker, triggering a strike by all workers. Furthermore, the company sent replacement workers to work, further escalating the conflict and resulting in multiple injuries. It is unknown whether this will be resolved soon.

Worker Dismissal

Since partnering with Moutai, Hong Kong & Whampoa Dockyard has many barges and employs many workers. Management is usually very strict. The day before yesterday at around 5:00 PM, a stoker on a small steamboat, named Yin Shenggeng, had a conflict with a colleague and ended up fighting. Afterwards, the Western manager, Vigro, learned about this and dismissed Yin and replaced him with Chen Are, who went to take over. Yin Shenggeng reported this to the Barge Workers' Union.

Strike Erupts

Hong Kong & Whampoa Dockyard has a total of 102 towboats and small steamboats, employing over 500 workers. They have organized a barge transport union, and all workers must join the union. When Yin Shenggeng was dismissed and the new worker, Chen Are, went to replace him, the workers believed that the company had dismissed the worker without notifying the union, and Chen Are was not a member of the union. Even if new workers were to be hired, union members should be given priority. The workers absolutely refused to accept Chen Are and demanded that the company rescind the decision to replace Yin Shenggeng. The company refused, so all the workers went on strike yesterday, and the strike has expanded.

Negotiation Process

The workers have already made demands and negotiated with Hong Kong & Whampoa Dockyard General Manager Vigro. The company authorities must earnestly fulfill the living conditions to protect workers, and any new workers hired by the company should be approved by the union and union members should be given priority. General Manager Vigro rejected the workers' demands, leading to a breakdown in negotiations. Yesterday morning at 11:00 AM, the General Labor Union, the Municipal Party Headquarters, etc., sent representatives Shen Fu (General Labor Union) and Huang Tiren (Municipal Party Headquarters) to the Barge Transport Union and the Hong Kong & Whampoa Dockyard Company to mediate.

Vigro's attitude was resolute, and there were no results.

Clash Erupts

Yesterday, all barge workers went on strike and were unable to work. The company then sent out more than ten reserve workers from General Manager Vigro to work on the barges. Vigro also told the workers that if they did not return to work by yesterday afternoon, the company would hire new workers. All the workers were united on this matter and refused to let the new workers board the barges. Yesterday at around 8:00 PM, more than ten new workers were sent to work on the barges and were beaten up by all the workers. One of the new workers, Jin Heshang, was seriously injured in the foot and managed to escape and seek treatment at the Tongren Hospital.

Many others were unable to escape and were beaten and injured. The situation is now deteriorating, and the company is unwilling to back down and has reported the incident to the police, who transported the injured to the hospital for treatment. As a result, goods being transferred between the company's ships have been blocked by the strike, causing enormous losses to the merchants.

List of Injured

The new workers who were beaten and injured include Chen Fugui, 37 years old, from Ningbo, whose legs were injured by iron bars; Wu Zongzhai, 35 years old, who injured his left leg; Zhou Xiaochun, 50 years old, who injured his head

and broke a rib; Hu Genfang, 30 years old, who injured his head. The above four were transported to Renji Hospital by Agent No. 8 from the Shuyao Police Station.

Then, the discussion of the following cases began: (1) Confidential; (2) The case of reporting the establishment of this committee and the elected committee members to the Municipal Party Headquarters for record was resolved and passed; (3) Not published; (4) The case of preventing the destruction of the entire organization and the use of coercive measures to reduce rent outside of contractual obligations was resolved as follows: A. Establish a legal advisory group; B. Retain the method; C. Hire Xue Dubi, Yu Hualong, Zhang Henghai, Wang Manyun, Zhang Tianbo, Zhang Juansheng, Cao Jie, Zhang Lishi, Lu Chao, Wang Zuxun, Yao Yuanding, Zheng Baozhang, Mao Fengwu, Ma Junshuo, Sun Biwu, Mao Yun, Li Caixia, Xue Chiping, Hong Weimei, Zhu Yakui, Zhu Yao, Feng Meixue, etc., as legal advisors; (5) The case of setting a date for convening a representative conference for discussion was resolved to hold it at 2:00 PM on the 26th of this month at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce; (6) The case of urging various organizations to separately convene rent reduction movement conferences and proceed unitedly was resolved to inform the various organizations that if they hold movement conferences, the date and location should be notified to this committee as soon as possible so that staff can be sent to guide; (7) The case of the Shoupinli and other tenant associations requesting assistance due to rent increases by landlords was resolved to reply separately, stating that rent increases or other coercive actions are not allowed during the rent reduction period; (8) The case of having standing committee members and secretaries on duty to facilitate progress was resolved to have office hours from 9:00 AM to 4:00 PM daily; (9) The case of using January 28th as the general mobilization for the rent reduction movement was resolved and passed. The meeting was adjourned.

Request for Record

The committee yesterday submitted a document to the Municipal Party Headquarters for record, stating, "Submitting the organization's process and the names of the elected committee members, requesting review and record. The organization of the association was initiated by the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and various industry guilds, the district branches of the First Special District Citizens' Federation, the General Labor Union, various hometown associations, and other organizations. On the 16th of this month, a joint conference of representatives was held at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce at 2:00 PM to discuss the issue of declining commerce in the city and providing relief to the people, discussing the issue of reducing rent. The representatives unanimously passed a resolution to establish

the Shanghai Municipal Rent Reduction Committee, and 35 people, including Ye Jiaxing (the list has been published in a previous newspaper), were elected as executive committee members. Furthermore, at 2:00 PM on the 20th of this month, the first executive committee was held to allocate responsibilities, electing Zhang Yichen, Ye Jiaxing, Wang Hanliang, Hu Fengxiang, Chen Binghui, Zhang Xianfang, Zhu Xuefan, Sun Mingqi, Zhou Funong as standing committee members, Cao Zhigong, Wang Honghui, Xue Guangqian as secretary directors, Zheng Dongshan, Xu Letian, Liang Gengshun as secretary deputy directors, Chen Jiufeng, Li Ruzhang as general affairs, Cai Qiajun, Wang Hesong as finance, Huang Xianggu, Zhu Yangwu as publicity, Zhang Dafu, Zhu Zhichun as organization, Liu Zhongying, Yuan Hongjun as investigation, and other departments. The undersigned submits the organization's process and the names of the elected committee members to your department for review. This matter concerns adjusting commercial difficulties and maintaining people's livelihoods. We hope that you will approve the record to promote the people's movement and facilitate progress. Please submit this to the Executive Committee of the Shanghai Special Municipality of the Kuomintang." The submitter is the Shanghai Municipal Rent Reduction Committee.

Sino-German Negotiations on State-Owned Steel Plant Reach Agreement

Ministry of Industries to Send More Personnel to Investigate Coal and Iron Nationwide

Regarding the Ministry of Industries' plan to establish a state-owned steel plant, Minister Chen Gongbo and representatives of the German Xiwang Third Company have negotiated several times in Nanjing and have reached an agreement. Details are as follows:

Plant Location Decided

The Ministry of Industries considers iron and coal to be the main conditions for establishing a steel plant and vital to the plant's future success. Therefore, before planning the establishment of the steel plant, experts were assigned to investigate the iron ore and coal production in various regions. After two years of research, it was determined that the Yangtze River Basin has rich iron and coal reserves and convenient transportation. Therefore, after negotiating with representatives of the German Xiwang Third Company in Nanjing, it was decided to locate the plant at Ma'anshan, near Dangtu. The coal will be sourced from the Gaokeng Coal Mine in Pingxiang, Jiangxi, for initial exploitation and use.

Iron and Coal Survey

After deciding on the location of the state-owned steel plant, the Ministry of Industries has begun preparations for various tasks. It is expected that some of the plant's work can begin in May or June. The Ministry recently, in order to clarify the amount of iron and coal reserves nationwide, will send more personnel to various provinces to conduct on-site surveys. According to previous surveys by foreigners, China's iron reserves total 766,899,000 tons (of which Liaoning accounts for 307,580,000 tons), and coal reserves total 997,604,000,000 tons. However, it is believed that the actual reserves nationwide must be twice this amount, because the previous surveys by foreigners only covered North China and the Northwest, while the Southwest provinces were not included.

Twenty-First Fiscal Year Postal Savings Bureau Business Report

Surplus of Over Two Million Seven Hundred Eighty Thousand Yuan

The Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau yesterday released its business report for the twenty-first fiscal year (July 1, 1932 to June 30, 1933). The year's surplus, after deducting the deposit for public reserve fund and special reserve fund of 836,508.72 yuan, totaled 1,951,853.67 yuan. All of it was transferred to the Postal Administration. The report is recorded below:

Annual Surplus: The total amount of the Savings and Remittance Bureau's loan balance sheet is 36,217,839.38 yuan. The asset portion includes: cash 14,951,383.07 yuan, exchange coupon reserve 2,200,000.00 yuan, investment 13,507,226.28 yuan, loans and overdrafts 3,278,145.88 yuan, accounts receivable and other funds 702,697.71 yuan, start-up costs 37,354.34 yuan, Postal Administration 239,941.63 yuan, collection on behalf of customers 55,713.00 yuan, term contract receivable 1,245,377.47 yuan, totaling the amount above. The liability portion includes: public reserve fund and special reserve fund 1,412,837.39 yuan, exchange coupon 2,200,000.00 yuan, remittances 3,585,418.18 yuan, savings deposits 25,397,057.71 yuan, accounts payable 278,810.77 yuan, miscellaneous deposits 522,689.52 yuan, amounts payable to various postal districts 1,510,935.34 yuan, collection on behalf of customers 55,713.00 yuan (i.e., the debit side collection item), term contract payable 1,245,377.47 yuan. In the profit and loss statement, the credit side (i.e., income) includes: remittance fees and water supply fees 3,093,070.38 yuan, net interest income from investments and discounts 1,525,528.95 yuan, net profit from insurance business 45,310.45 yuan, and other income items 3,941.73 yuan, totaling 4,667,851.51 yuan. The debit side (i.e., losses) includes: various expenses of the General Administration and the Shanghai, Beijing, and Hankou branch offices 702,069.37 yuan, appropriation for exchange losses, commissions, and handling fees 632,797.83 yuan, start-up costs 19,621.92 yuan, management fees 525,000.00 yuan, totaling 1,879,489.12 yuan. The net surplus between the two is 2,788,362.39 yuan.

Savings Business: (1) Passbook Savings: The total amount deposited throughout the year was 25,446,818.48 yuan, and the total amount withdrawn was 26,019,336.95 yuan. Compared with the previous year's deposits of 31,115,380.26 yuan and withdrawals of 30,250,772.93 yuan, this is a decrease of approximately 18% and 14% respectively. The year-end balance was 20,339,325.70 yuan, a decrease of approximately 3% compared to the previous year's 21,007,925.09 yuan. The total number of savings accounts was 145,166, an increase of approximately 2% compared to the previous year's 143,009 accounts. The average deposit per account was 140 yuan. (2) Fixed Deposit Savings: The total amount deposited throughout the year was 3,082,484.60 yuan, and the total amount withdrawn was 3,427,689.36 yuan. Compared with the previous year's deposits of 3,636,179.62 yuan and withdrawals of 1,652,909.00 yuan, the former decreased by approximately 15% and the latter increased by approximately 107%. The year-end balance was 3,985,376.79 yuan, a decrease of approximately 8% compared to the previous year's 4,334,017.17 yuan. The total number of savings accounts was 5,097, a decrease of approximately 7% compared to the previous year's 5,464 accounts. The average savings per account was 782 yuan. (3) Checking Account Savings: The total amount deposited throughout the year was 18,797,181.25 yuan, and the total amount withdrawn was 19,542,654.41 yuan. Compared with the previous year's deposits of 22,258,699.01 yuan and withdrawals of 22,407,253.29 yuan, this is a decrease of approximately 16% and 13% respectively. The year-end balance was 1,072,355.22 yuan, a decrease of approximately 41% compared to the previous year's 1,822,804.08 yuan.

Remittance Business: (A) Domestic Remittances: (1) Money Orders: The total amount issued throughout the year was 164,849,000 yuan, a decrease of approximately 10% compared to the previous year's 183,716,100 yuan. (2) Airmail Money Orders: The total amount issued throughout the year was 1,237,800 yuan, an increase of approximately 8% compared to the previous year's 1,141,400 yuan. (3) Telegraphic Transfers: Business began in February 1933, and the total amount issued by the end of June was 44,000 yuan. (4) Small Amount Money Orders: The total amount issued throughout the year was 1,679,800 yuan, an increase of approximately 21% compared to the previous year's 1,388,700 yuan. (5) Collection of Goods Payments: The total revenue throughout the year was 3,082,900 yuan, an increase of approximately 16% compared to the previous year's 2,657,700 yuan. (6) Collection of Registered Mail Payments: The total revenue throughout the year was 23,000 yuan, an increase of approximately 32% compared to the previous year's 17,400 yuan. (B) Foreign Remittances: (1) Money Orders: The total amount issued throughout the year was 1,431,660.58 yuan, a decrease of approximately 13% compared to the previous year's 1,645,369.43 yuan. The total amount paid out was 1,979,886.11 yuan, an increase of approximately 29% compared to the previous year's 2,791,647.53 yuan. (2) Collection of Parcel Payments: The total amount issued throughout the year was 511,765.29 yuan, a decrease of approximately 18% compared to the previous year's 621,425.24 yuan. The total amount paid out was 10,250.34 yuan, a decrease of approximately 52% compared to the previous year's 21,303.15 yuan. (3) Collection of Registered Mail Payments: The total amount issued throughout the year was 80,771.90 yuan, a decrease of approximately 29% compared to the previous year's 113,219.01 yuan. The total amount paid out was 794.47 yuan, a decrease of approximately 73% compared to the previous year's 2,893.82 yuan.

Business Overview: The total amount of domestic remittances for the twenty-first fiscal year decreased by approximately 10% compared to the previous year, and remittance income decreased by approximately 17%. The total amount of savings deposits also decreased by 6%. This is because after the fall of four provinces, the Ministry of Communications issued a clear order to blockade postal areas, resulting in significant losses for postal remittances. Furthermore, the unrest in Sichuan and Shandong provinces, the communist disaster in Jiangxi, the drought in Shanxi, and the war in northern Hebei all had a significant impact. However, the Bureau continued to work hard to develop postal remittance services. For example, the telegraphic transfer service, which began in February of last year, had a substantial amount of 44,000 yuan in just five months. This result is quite remarkable. Therefore, looking at the results of the above-mentioned remittance services, except for domestic remittances, the rest have shown significant progress. The decline in the total amount of domestic remittances is due to the decrease in the issuance of money orders. The small amount money order business is still showing satisfactory results, with an increase of approximately 82% compared to the previous year. This business is now expanding to various postal agencies, which is quite beneficial to the development of commerce in the interior. As for the decline in savings deposits, most of it is due to the decrease in checking account savings in the Shanghai and Nanjing areas, while passbook savings accounts and fixed deposit savings accounts have decreased less. Due to the impact of the war in the Beiping and Hebei areas, passbook savings deposits decreased by as much as 2 million yuan, but there is still a trend of increase in other areas. Furthermore, although the assets of the post office in the four northeastern provinces that were occupied are ten times greater than the savings deposits, the post office still recognizes the claims of all depositors and allows them to be cashed out. Before the end of that fiscal year, depositors had already received 50% of the total amount.

Financial Circles Plan to Establish Ammonium Sulfate Manufacturing Plant

Resisting Japanese Monopoly of the Market

Based on Yongli Company

Ammonium sulfate is a major modern chemical industrial product. In peacetime, it is used as fertilizer for farmland, and in wartime, it can be used to manufacture military supplies. According to reliable surveys, the annual consumption of ammonium sulfate in Japanese farmland reaches more than 620,000 tons. The use of artificial fertilizers by farmers in our country is not yet developed. Although our farmland area is ten times that of Japan, the annual consumption is only more than 150,000 tons. It is expected that after the improvement of agriculture in the future, the demand for ammonium sulfate will be unlimited. Examining various countries, all are striving for self-sufficiency in this item. In recent years, the number of ammonium sulfate manufacturing plants in Japan has increased to eleven, with an investment of 600 million yen, which seems to have reached a level sufficient for self-sufficiency. Recently, in our country's lost territory, the Manchurian Chemical Industry Company was established, with a capital of 25 million yen, half of which was received first. In April of last year, construction began in Dalian to build an ammonium sulfate plant, which is scheduled to be completed in November of this year. Recently, it has been heard that the work is being accelerated, and it may be completed within October. The plant is expected to produce approximately 180,000 tons annually. In the future, it will not only be self-sufficient, but will also dump its products in our country, monopolizing the East Asian market. It is heard that Chinese chemical industrialist Fan Xudong, and members of the financial community in this city Zhang Gongquan, Zhou Zuomin, Chen Guangfu, Xu Xinliu, and others, in view of the urgency of establishing a plant to produce artificial fertilizer themselves, and seeing the success of the Yongli Company's alkali production business, decided to establish an ammonium sulfate manufacturing plant based on that company. It is heard that the plan has been finalized. Chinese people, seeing the rapid progress of the Japanese in building industries in our lost territory, should know that we are lagging behind and must catch up quickly.

Telephone Line to be Added Between Nanjing and Shanghai

The National Economic Commission believes that the Nanjing-Shanghai Highway is of great importance to transportation between Nanjing and Shanghai, so it has specially sent a letter to the Ministry of Communications to instruct the Directorate General of Telecommunications to plan to install a long-distance telephone line along the road, which will begin construction soon. This long-distance telephone line will start from Nanjing, pass through Jurong, Yixing, Wuxi, Changshu, Taicang, and Jiading, and reach Shanghai. The entire line is 232 miles long and will be installed with four pairs of number 10 steel wires. In addition to ordinary cross-connection, a carrier system will be added so that six telephone lines can be obtained on four wires. Materials are currently being prepared, and installation will begin in Nanjing within the next few days. It is expected to be completed and operational by early April. The total cost of the line is approximately 500,000 yuan. From then on, transportation between Nanjing and Shanghai will become more convenient.

Municipal Public Works Bureau Completes Pudong Water Plant Project

Plant Site and Water Source Surveyed and Determined at Youlong Pier in Yangjing District

Total Cost of 300,000 Yuan, Cooperation Between Government and Business Investment

Construction Can Begin Within This Year, Water Supply Expected in About One Year

The establishment of a water plant in Pudong was planned and designed by the municipal authorities beginning in the 18th year of the Republic. The entire plan has been completed by the Municipal Public Works Bureau. More than 100 mu of land near the British-American Tobacco Company in Pudong has been purchased, and the Pudong Youlong Pier has been surveyed and determined as the water source for the water plant. The total cost is 300,000 yuan, and a meeting will be held to decide the details in the next few days. Once the date of construction is determined, it is expected that water can be supplied in about one year. The Shin Shi News Agency reporter specially visited Mr. Chen, the Section Chief of the Second Division of the Public Works Bureau, yesterday to inquire about the planning process and the current status. The details are recorded as follows:

Design Process

According to the municipal authorities' plan to build a water plant in Pudong, the project began in the 18th year of the Republic. At that time, the Pudong market was gradually becoming prosperous, and the number of residents was increasing daily. Most of the rivers were silted up, and the residents' drinking water was very unclean. This was not only harmful to the health of the people, but also in the event of a fire, there was no water supply for fire fighting, which could easily lead to conflagration. Local residents and health authorities felt that it was necessary to establish a water plant immediately. They jointly suggested this to the municipal government, and the then Mayor Zhang Yuejun also believed that the establishment of a water plant in Pudong was indeed urgent. He immediately ordered the Finance Bureau to allocate 80,000 yuan to the Municipal Public Works Bureau to actively prepare.

Purchase of Plant Site

After receiving the order, the Municipal Public Works Bureau immediately began to handle the matter separately. However, the search for a plant site was quite difficult because the site had to take into account the environment and also have a better water source. The water sources on the banks of the Pudong Yangjing District were mostly turbid and unsuitable for use. Recently, a site near the Youlong Pier, diagonally opposite the Tongren Pier in Puxi, has been found to be relatively suitable. At the same time, in between the Taikoo Wharf and the EWO Wharf nearby, there is a vacant land of more than 100 mu, which is sufficient for use. If necessary, the nearby area can be expanded to build water towers and other buildings. It was purchased for a price of more than 10,000 yuan. At the same time, an agreement was reached with the Municipal Ferry Management Office to cede the Youlong Pier for dredging and use as a water source.

Fundraising

The first phase of the water plant project requires 300,000 yuan. In addition to the 80,000 yuan previously allocated during Mayor Zhang's tenure, the remaining 200,000 yuan is still needed to carry out the construction. The 80,000 yuan that had been allocated, except for about 20,000 yuan spent on land purchase and design, was taken back by the Municipal Finance Bureau and used for other purposes during the "January 28th" Shanghai Incident because the municipal treasury was in financial difficulty. As a result, the water plant, which was about to begin construction, had to be suspended temporarily. Now, the municipal authorities, in response to the needs of the facts and the requests of the gentry and directors of Pudong, have decided to implement the project in the shortest possible time. Moreover, the current total donations of foreign merchants' warehouses, factories, etc. in Pudong are often withheld or not paid on the pretext of inadequate municipal public facilities. If the water plant is established, the amount of taxes that can be recovered is no less than tens of thousands of yuan. The Pudong market can also become more prosperous as a result, and the increase in land value tax, calculated on the basis of 4,000 mu in the Yangjing District, is also considerable. The municipal authorities will also indirectly benefit from this. However, recently, the municipal government still does not have such a large amount of money available for the time being. In order to allocate funds for construction as soon as possible, Mayor Wu recently convened a meeting of Pudong gentry and the banking community in this city to discuss loan methods. Yao Mulian, Kui Yanfang, Lin Kanghou, Pan Zhifang, Cai Zengji, Xu Peihuang, and others have been appointed as members of the committee, and a meeting will be convened in the next few days to decide on the method. It is heard that a satisfactory solution is expected to be reached in the short term and construction will begin.

Date of Water Supply

According to Mr. Chen, who is in charge of the preparation of the plant, everything related to the internal construction and equipment of the plant has been designed and drawn. Procedures such as bidding for construction have also been prepared. The selection of machinery, the route of the water pipes, and the procedures for ordering and contracting have all been drafted. Now, only the funding needs to be resolved. As soon as the funding is resolved, we can start dredging the water source and building the plant, and order machinery from abroad. The entire project can be completed in at most one year.

Prominent Dye Merchant Fan Aisheng Kidnapped

Shantou Road Pre-Parked Ice 539 Car

Kidnappers Snatched Fan into the Car and Speeded Away

｜｜ Chauffeur Franticly Went Home to Report｜｜

Fan Aisheng, 47 years old, from Jiangyin, resides at No. 31 Songshan Road. He made his fortune in the dye business and has accumulated a huge fortune. He occupies a prominent position among dye merchants. However, Fan is frugal by nature, so he lives very simply. Even when he goes out every day, he only hires a chartered car. At 7:45 p.m. yesterday, Fan had a social engagement, so he took his chartered car to Shantou Road. Unexpectedly, when the car reached the intersection of Shantou Road and Guangxi Road, four bandits suddenly jumped out of the roadside. Two bandits were empty-handed, and two bandits were armed with guns. They blocked Fan's car and threatened the driver to stop. The driver had no choice but to stop the car. The four bandits then went forward together, grabbed Fan, and prohibited him from making any noise. They dragged him into a public concession registration No. 6539 black plate car that was parked on the roadside, and sped away. At that time, Fan's driver, seeing his master being kidnapped, was frantic and dared not make any noise, fearing that his master's life would be endangered. After the bandits' car drove far away, he rushed home to report and reported to the Old Gate Police Station, requesting assistance. After receiving the report, the police station immediately dispatched detectives to the scene of the incident to investigate. They searched in all directions, but there were no clues as of midnight. At the same time, the bandits' car was not found. Therefore, the police station notified all municipal police agencies, requesting their assistance.

Murderous Plot Against Elementary School Student Wang Deyu Sentenced to Death

Zhou Ayuan Acquitted

Ding Yin, a 49-year-old woman from Wuxi, the owner of Ding Juxing Iron Shop at No. 658 Xiaoshadu Road, Shanghai West, is a widow and has a 13-year-old only son, Ding Fugeng, who studies at the Ba Xianqiao Sino-French School in the French Concession. Because the school is far away and inconvenient to travel back and forth every day, he boards at his aunt's house at No. 123 Laohe Road. Wang Deyu, 26 years old, is the son of the deceased husband's brother who married into the family. He also worked in the iron shop business. Because of his bad behavior, he lost his job and was unemployed. He often asked Ms. Yin for loans, but Ms. Yin refused to associate with him because she could not bear the trouble. Unexpectedly, Deyu held a grudge from then on. Seeing that Ms. Yin had dozens of acres of good farmland, houses, and shops in her hometown, he wanted to seize this property. Because Ms. Yin had a biological son, Fugeng, it was difficult to achieve his goal, so he had the idea of murdering Fugeng. In October of last year, while Ms. Yin was back in her hometown, on the 25th of the same month, Deyu waited in front of the Sino-French School at noon. When he saw Fugeng leaving school, he stepped forward and falsely claimed to Fugeng, "Your mother is in the countryside and sent me to call you back to the countryside." Fugeng was young and ignorant and fell for his trick. He was lured to the cotton fields next to the Xuan family's residence in Longhua Airport and killed by Zhou Ayuan (the same age as Deyu), a Jiangyin native who lived at No. 1 Zhangjiabang Road, Jumen Road, Shanghai South, and worked in the same industry. The body was abandoned in the wilderness and the perpetrators fled. After the incident, the body was identified by the land protector and the Shanghai District Court. Later, the body was claimed by the mother, and detectives from the Public Security Bureau first arrested the accomplice Zhou Ayuan. According to Zhou's confession, they went to Nanxiang and arrested the principal offender Wang Deyu and brought him back to Shanghai. The French police believed that the location where the deceased was lured was within the French Concession, so they immediately transferred the two criminals, Wang and Zhou, to the case and sent them to the Second Special District Court. The police lawyer filed a public prosecution against them for the crime of premeditated murder under Article 284 of the Criminal Code. The details of the interrogation have been recorded in previous reports. It is now understood that this case was originally presided over by Judge Zhang Chaozuo. Later, because Mr. Zhang was transferred to the Third Branch of the High Court, it was taken over by Judge Wu Fanglian. Later, Mr. Wu, out of caution, repeatedly reopened the debate and conducted a thorough investigation in order to avoid injustice. This case has been tried and concluded, and yesterday was the date of sentencing. At 10:00 a.m., Judge Wu appeared in court and ordered the two criminals to be brought to the court. The main text of the judgment stated: Wang Deyu, for premeditated murder, is sentenced to death and deprived of public rights indefinitely. Zhou Ayuan is acquitted. Police lawyer Fei Xizhen requested that Zhou Ayuan be temporarily detained during the appeal period. The court approved the request and ordered the two defendants to be transferred to the detention center to await further instructions during the appeal period.

International Savings Society vs. Gold Exchange Chess Match

Twenty-Four to Sixteen: Gold Exchange Wins

The Shanghai YMCA held its third annual chess competition. The most outstanding team was the International Savings Society. Jiangsu-Zhejiang-Anhui Unified Tax Bureau Discovers Embezzlement Case Involving Over 80,000

Forging Director's Signature and Illegally Engraving Director's Seal

Clerk Deng Darong Has Been Detained and Sent to Court for Trial

According to Da Gong She, the Jiangsu-Zhejiang-Anhui Unified Tax Bureau of this city, during the year-end tax settlement for the 22nd year of the Republic, suddenly discovered a major case involving Deng Darong, a second-class clerk of the bureau, who forged the director's seal to fraudulently obtain a large sum of tax money from the Central Bank. Deng has now been detained and sent to court to await legal sanctions. The Da Gong She reporter received the news and went to the Unified Tax Bureau on Chengdu Road to interview Chen Yan'yin, the head of the First Section, and learned the details of the case as follows:

Embezzlement Discovered During Year-End Reconciliation

The Jiangsu-Zhejiang-Anhui Unified Tax Bureau has management offices and inspection offices. Taxes collected by the management offices are directly submitted to the Tax Affairs Department, and the amount submitted is reported to the bureau. Taxes collected by the inspection offices are directly submitted by manufacturers in various locations to the Central Bank or its branches, with bank receipts submitted to the offices, which then report to the bureau. At the end of last year, the bureau reconciled accounts with the Central Bank. Due to the bank's busy year-end settlement, there was no time for detailed verification. It was not until January 4th of this year that both parties reconciled clearly. Although the amount collected and submitted on the books was accurate, the tax certificates issued by the bureau were short by 84,321.21 yuan. Therefore, it was discovered that there must be fraud involved. The bureau quietly investigated and found that Deng Darong, a second-class clerk, had privately engraved a seal, forged checks, and fraudulently obtained tax money.

Extravagant Behavior Arouses Suspicion

Deng Darong is from Jiangxi and has been a second-class clerk in the bureau for about two years, handling tax remittance documents in the cashier's section. He usually behaves extravagantly and spends lavishly. Even the secretary and section chief of the bureau, who earns more than Deng, does not have Deng's air. The director of the bureau, Wang Zongmo, had already become suspicious. In mid-December of last year, he transferred Chen Yan'yin, the secretary, to be the head of the First Section, instructing him to investigate the accounts and pay attention to any irregularities. This was because of the year-end reconciliation with the Central Bank. Otherwise, the bureau's dealings with the Central Bank only require monthly reconciliations, and there would be no detailed reconciliation. Furthermore, Deng's leave of absence to Guangdong at the end of the year further aroused suspicion among the bureau's staff.

Returns from Leave and is Detained and Sent to Court

Although Deng Darong is from Jiangxi, his family is in Guangdong. At the end of last year, Deng suddenly took sick leave to return to Guangdong, initially planning to return to Shanghai on the 4th of this year, but later informed that he would return on the 6th. At this time, the bureau had already discovered Deng's embezzlement, so when Deng arrived in Shanghai from Guangdong on the 6th, senior officials of the bureau went to the dock to meet him. As soon as Deng landed, he was invited to meet the director at the Tax Affairs Department on the Bund (because Director Wang also served as the director of the Tax Affairs Department). He was severely questioned about everything. Deng initially denied it, but when he was shown the forged checks from the Central Bank, he bowed his head and had nothing to say. Deng was immediately sent to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for detention, and the bureau transferred him to the court for interrogation. The prosecutor has already opened an investigative court once.

Mysterious and Clever Method of Fraud

The cashier's section of the bureau has always withdrawn money by having the head of the cashier's section write the amount to be withdrawn on the check and submit it to Director Wang for his personal signature and seal before it can be withdrawn from the Central Bank. Deng was responsible for handling tax remittance documents in the cashier's section, so he sometimes wrote the checks on behalf of the section chief. Deng secretly paid attention to the director's seal and signature style for fraudulent use. His method of embezzlement was to retain tax money for his own use. "For example, this month, Hangzhou remitted 10,000 yuan in cotton tax, 10,000 yuan in cement tax, and 10,000 yuan in match tax to the bureau, totaling 30,000 yuan. Deng used a forged check to withdraw this amount from the Central Bank, and the remittance documents were temporarily set aside. When other provinces remitted tax money in the following month, the previous tax money would be replenished, and then the remittance documents would be made and reported." However, the amount remitted by various provinces sometimes had odd fractions of a few jiao and fen, so Deng sometimes had to deposit cash into the bank to match the amounts between the Unified Tax Bureau and the Central Bank. Therefore, during the monthly reconciliation, the amounts reconciled by both parties were accurate, and the embezzlement was not discovered for a year. This was due to such sleight of hand. As for the source of Deng's blank checks, he obtained them by fraud in the check request form in the checkbook and fraudulently obtained them from the bank.

Search of Deng's Residence Reveals Some Remaining Funds

Deng Darong's residence in Shanghai is at 19 Kangle Village, Fuxu Road. The court has sent judicial police to search the residence and found 11,000 yuan in cash in the Kenyee Bank, as well as several thousand yuan in other property. The rest of the fraudulently obtained money has been squandered by Deng. As for whether there is any other property in Guangdong, it is currently unknown.

Director of Unified Tax Bureau Voluntarily Requests Punishment

Finally, according to Chen Yan'yin, the head of the First Section of the bureau, told the Da Gong She reporter that at the beginning of the incident, it was mostly suspected that many people were involved. It was not until Deng Darong confessed that it was Deng alone who embezzled, and no one else was involved. As for the Central Bank's oversight, because it and the Tax Bureau are both agencies of the Ministry of Finance, this loss can be considered common. However, Director Wang has voluntarily requested punishment for negligence due to his official duties.

Seven Maids Poisoned by Coal Gas

Six Rescued, One Dies

In the residence of Wang E'zeng, a secretary of the Naval Survey Bureau from Fuzhou, located at 72 Mingde Lane, Dingxu Road, French Concession, seven maids were employed: Da Wu, Xiao Wu, Ling Ma, Chen Ma, Zhou Ma, Wang Ma, and Liu Ma. There were also several male servants, all from Anhui. At night, the seven maids slept in the attic. The night before last (22nd), because the weather was cold, each maid used a tin garbage can to ignite coal briquettes and place them in the room for heating. After everyone fell asleep, they were all suffocated by coal gas. At 8:30 yesterday morning, the owner saw that the maids had not gotten up and knocked on the door for a long time. There was no response from the room, arousing suspicion. The male servant Liu Fubao pried open the door and entered, filled with coal gas. The maids were all unconscious, breathing weakly, and on the verge of death. The employer immediately ordered an urgent report to the police, and they were taken to Guangci Hospital for treatment. Among the seven maids, Zhou Ma (around 30 years old) died due to severe poisoning at around 10 o'clock. The rest were rescued and survived. The hospital notified the police, and Detective Zhang Chunsheng was sent to investigate. The body was transported to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch autopsy center. It was found that the deceased had no family members in Shanghai, and a report will be made to the Second Special District Court today to send personnel for inspection.

Guangfu Xing Game Shop Carelessness Investigated as Arson, Seeking Compensation

Jin Yongchang Confesses Conspiracy Details

Shop Owner and Other Related Parties Arrested

Guangfu Xing Game Shop at 163 Yunnan Road suddenly caught fire at 4:35 AM the day before yesterday. Dense smoke filled the air, and the fire was extremely fierce. Soon, it broke through the roof. After the fire brigades from various sections tried their best to extinguish the fire, 163 was completely burned down, and the adjacent 161 and 165 were also severely damaged. Afterwards, the Laozha Police Station ordered Chinese Detectives Yang Dechun and He Chengrui to investigate the source of the fire. A man named Jin Yongchang from this region came forward and confessed. When the detectives asked how the fire started, Jin said, "I live in the attic of the house. Before the fire, I got up to urinate and accidentally knocked over the kerosene stove. The kerosene flowed from the floor into the coal briquette basin downstairs, causing the fire." The detectives found many loopholes in Jin's confession and took him to the police station for strict interrogation. Jin finally revealed the truth, saying that the owners of Guangfu Xing, Fan Guanglai and Fan Zhongyan from Chongming, had taken out fire insurance with the Shanghai Reiss & Co. Insurance Department of the German merchant in November last year, totaling 8,600 yuan. At that time, Guo Xichou said that if there was a fire, he would be able to find a way to obtain compensation, but Guo would deduct 40%. Two weeks ago, Fan invited me to discuss the plan to commit arson. He instructed me to start the fire upstairs first, and they would light nine small baskets filled with waste paper and soaked in gasoline downstairs, one by one. After it was done, they promised to reward me with 50 yuan. Yesterday, I carried out this plan." The detectives then separately arrested the two Fans and Guo, as well as the shop assistants Chen Yuanlang and the apprentice Yao Chuanlang, and detained them. Last night, they were sent to the First Special Court's Criminal Division. The police station's lawyer Li Zhishan presented the case, prosecuting them for the crime of public endangerment under Article 187 of the Criminal Law, and stated that the case still needs to be investigated and requested a postponement of the trial. Qian Hongye, the head of the Criminal Division, verified the report, briefly questioned each defendant, and ordered a change of date for further verification.

Yangtze River Water Level Drops Sharply, Navigational Routes Above and Below Stream Are Severed into Four Sections

Yangtze River Line Requires Transshipment at Wuhu

Hunan Line Requires Transshipment at Xindi

The Yangtze River water level this year is shallow and dropping rapidly. Initially, it dropped four or five feet, then suddenly dropped more than ten feet. Yesterday, the downstream water level further decreased by more than one foot, while the upstream water level sharply dropped to five feet. Shanghai-bound river steamers to Hankou, larger vessels, can only load one-quarter of their capacity, and navigation above and below stream is extremely difficult. The details are as follows:

Water Level Drops Again Yesterday, the various shipping companies received a telegram from Hankou stating that on the 22nd, the downstream Yangtze River water level had sharply decreased by more than one foot. The current highest point has dropped from 11 feet 5 inches to 10 feet 4 inches. The Jianghan Customs notified all ships that the draft for upstream cargo should not exceed 10 feet, and the water level is continuing to decrease. The Taiziji and Xiaogushan areas downstream are even shallower, making it extremely difficult for river steamers to navigate.

Blocked into Two Sections The Yangtze River, from Shanghai to Hankou, is blocked at Wuhu. All river steamers with a draft of 11 feet cannot pass through the area. In the past few days, six or seven vessels have been stranded in Wuhu due to the shallow water. Yesterday, the Songpu of Sanbei was again unable to sail upstream due to the water level dropping to 10 feet 4 inches. It transshipped 2,700 pieces of cargo at Wuhu using barges and then managed to pass. Other shipping companies' river steamers also transship at Wuhu. Furthermore, yesterday the upstream water level to Changsha dropped to five feet. Ships going upstream from Hankou can only reach Chenglingji, then use small boats to tow barges to transfer cargo. Cargo going downstream from Changsha is also transshipped to ships at that location. The upstream and downstream routes have been divided into four sections for navigation.

Cargo Congestion The Yangtze River lines, whether upstream or downstream, except for shallow-water vessels, larger ships have followed the Jianghan Customs' notification since the 20th, reducing their loading capacity. River steamers over 3,000 tons can only load 25% to 30% of their cargo, resulting in a large accumulation of incoming goods in Hunan and Hankou. Many passengers plan to arrive in Shanghai within the next three weeks, so they are requesting various companies to add shallow-water vessels to increase cargo capacity. The China Merchants Bureau's Hankou branch has also requested the Shanghai Bureau to transfer two shallow-water sea vessels to Hankou to transport cargo, and has requested that the Kuaili be rerouted to Shanghai-Hankou to quickly carry passengers and cargo.

Surcharge Tomorrow The Yangtze River shallow-water surcharge, agreed upon by six companies, will be increased by 15% starting tomorrow, with a deadline of March 15th. The various shipping companies, due to the poor business conditions of the Yangtze River and the plummeting freight rates, have delayed the collection of the shallow-water surcharge compared to last year. However, it is heard that the companies will still collect the 15% shallow-water surcharge at 95% of the usual freight rate.

City Chamber of Commerce Requests Stamp Tax Bureau to Change the Stamp Duty Period for Account Books

Because the Closing Period is in February

The City Chamber of Commerce, based on joint letters from various industry guilds, requested the Shanghai Stamp Tax Bureau to allow businesses to stamp their account books in February of each year to avoid misunderstandings. Yesterday, it specifically forwarded a letter stating, "We received letters from the Rice Industry, Native Cloth Industry, Pollen Industry, Lumber Industry, Tobacco and Alcohol Industry, Seafood Industry, Cosmetics Industry, Chinese and Foreign Sundries Industry, Silk Thread and Sock Dyeing Industry, Fresh Medicine Industry, Jewelry Industry, Tea and Ink Industry, Hat Shop Industry, Leather and Wool Hat Industry, Noodle Restaurant Industry, Medical Wine Shop Industry, Blacksmith Industry, Construction Factory Industry, Seafood Sundries Industry, Sugar and Longan Industry, Flour Mill Industry, Tobacco Leaf Industry, Cotton Shop Industry, Machine Dyeing and Weaving Industry, Knitting Industry, Department Store Industry, and Electrical Appliance Manufacturing Industry Associations stating that the account books used by businesses are stamped annually per volume in accordance with the Provisional Stamp Tax Regulations promulgated by the National Government, but the business accounting year has long been ordered by the Executive Yuan to be closed at the end of January of the following year, so businesses must change to new books in February at the same time as stamping. This is a long-standing habit in the business community. If you want to replace the new book before the final account, it is difficult to implement, and it is an unexpected burden to restamp the book for one year, and there is no legal basis for it. Therefore, the date of affixing the new stamps for this year's book should be set to start from February 15th. If there are any unused books from last year, they should be affixed with one jiao stamp when used in February 15th of this year to comply with the regulations. We jointly request your association to review and quickly forward the letter to the Shanghai Stamp Tax Bureau for approval and processing, and to inform the inspectors in each district to avoid misunderstandings, and hope to see a reply," etc. The commercial year-end closing is ordered to be the end of January of the following year, then changing to a new book or using an old book, and stamping it, is always in February of the Gregorian calendar. The request to affix the stamp starting from February 15th is to avoid misunderstandings during inspection. We hereby request your bureau to check and notify the inspectors to avoid misunderstandings, and hope to see a reply. This is to the utmost importance. This is addressed to the Jiangsu Shanghai Stamp Tax Bureau.

Seamen's Union Mediates Shanghai Lun's Work Stoppage; Work Resumes Immediately

The Ship Sailed Yesterday Morning

Four Measures Established

The Shanghai Lun, a ship of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company leased to the China Merchants Bureau, with a total of sixty-eight workers, had a work stoppage due to the company's unwarranted dismissal of workers. After the Seamen's Union mediated overnight, work was resumed late the night before. The details are as follows:

Overnight Mediation The workers in various departments of the ship had been opposing the company's deduction of wages and dismissal of all workers in the seamen's department. Repeated mediation by the union was ineffective. Therefore, at 3:30 PM the day before, all workers in various departments stopped working and declared a work stoppage. Persuasion by personnel from the Seamen's General Union and branch unions was ineffective. At 8:00 PM the night before, Ye Chuanfang, the company's manager, personally went to the union to negotiate. The union then summoned Wang Yongfa, the representative of the dismissed seamen, for mediation. Cheng Deyuan from the General Union and Si Shijian from the branch union attended until late at night, when a resolution was finally reached.

Four Measures The Seamen's Branch repeatedly persuaded both parties and decided on four measures: (1) One and a half months' salary will be paid to the former seamen Wang Yongfa, etc. All of Wang Yongfa's insurance policies will be cancelled. (2) The company will assist the Seamen's Union in persuading current seamen who have not joined the union to join. (3) In the future, the company should provide reasons and seek the union's consent one week before dismissing workers. (4) In the future, when there are vacancies on the company's ships, the union must recommend candidates for employment, but without signing a contract.

Work Resumes and Departs The sixty-eight workers in the firemen, sailors, stevedores, and hold departments of the ship were satisfied with the resolution. Representatives from the Seamen's Union and Seamen's Branch boarded the ship to urge them to resume work immediately. All the workers resumed work late at night, and the ship departed as usual yesterday morning, sailing to Qingdao. The work stoppage was resolved.

China Merchants Bureau Prepares to Launch Special Express Steamer Between Beijing and Hankou

To Launch After Kuaili Completes Its Assignment

Beijing-Shanghai Railway Plans Joint Steamer Transportation

According to the Xin Sheng News Agency, after Zhang Yanxiang, director of the Navigation Administration Office of the Hubei Provincial Construction Department, suggested launching a special express steamer between Beijing and Hankou, the state-owned China Merchants Bureau has been preparing, and the two Railway Administrations are preparing to handle joint transportation. The details are as follows:

China Merchants Prepares

Liu Hongsheng, the general manager of the China Merchants Bureau, instructed He Molin, the chief of the business department, and Zhao Yuntai, the chief of the shipbuilding department, to formulate a plan for launching the special express steamer between Hankou and Nanjing, as well as the schedule and price list. He also designated the Emei river steamer to sail. However, the Emei ran aground in Fuzhou. After rescue efforts failed, it is still stranded on the reef, causing the plan to launch the special express steamer between Beijing and Hankou to be suspended. Now, the bureau plans to send the Kuaili river steamer, but the Kuaili is still on assignment, and there is no launch date for the time being.

Two Railways Study

The Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administrations submitted Zhang Yanxiang's proposal for the express steamer to the traffic department for study of joint transportation measures. Now, Zheng Baozhao of the traffic department has formulated the measures: (1) Sign a contract with the steamer bureau (or company) to issue joint tickets between major stations on both railways, as well as Anqing, Jiujiang, and Hankou. (2) Contact the Pinghan Railway, Nanxun Railway, and Yuehan Railway's Hunan-Hubei section to discuss all joint transportation procedures. (3) Set the fare and pre-define all joint transportation prices. (4) Set the validity period for one-way and round-trip joint tickets. (5) Stipulate the free baggage weight and excess baggage charges. (6) Transportation procedures, such as if the express steamer stops at Xiaguan, passengers and their luggage from the Beijing Station of this railway to the steamer wharf must be transported by motor vehicle. This motor vehicle can be purchased by the railway, jointly operated by both parties, or contracted by the China Merchants Bureau. How the expenses will be distributed and whether this transportation fee should be added to the joint ticket must be negotiated. (7) Wharf facilities, such as if the express steamer docks at the Nanjing Jiangbian Station wharf of this railway, the above procedures can be waived, and passengers will find it more convenient. However, all facilities on the wharf must be fully arranged. (8) Contact the customs to discuss matters related to the inspection of luggage. (10) Publicize the implementation of this measure vigorously to attract customers.

Current Status

According to the report from the traffic department of the two railways on the current status of joint transportation between Beijing and Hankou: (1) Joint transportation from Shanghai to Hankou has long been implemented. According to the current schedule, it takes a total of 61 hours and 25 minutes from Shanghai to Beijing, via Xuzhou and Zhengzhou, to Hankou. The joint transportation ticket price is 81.6 yuan for first class, 52.7 yuan for second class, and 26.35 yuan for third class (including the surcharge for the special express train and the ferry fee, but not including the sleeper fee for first and second class). (2) Two years before the founding of the Republic, the two railways signed a joint transportation contract with the China Merchants Bureau and Jardine Matheson, Taikoo, and Nisshin shipping companies. Passengers traveling from Shanghai to Hankou or from Hankou to Shanghai who wish to take a passenger train on the Beijing-Shanghai section can declare in advance and take the passenger train of this railway at the Shanghai and Beijing stations with the voucher issued by the bureaus and companies. After the joint transportation of each railway was implemented, domestic tour tickets were issued, traveling from Shanghai to Beijing, via the Tianjin-Pukou Line and the Beijing-Shenyang Line to Beijing, then from the Beijing-Hankou Line, from Beijing to Hankou, and taking a steamer from Hankou to Shanghai. (2) The Beijing-Wu highway is now under construction. The two railways have consulted with the Beijing-Wu Highway Long-Distance Bus Preparation Office of the Jiangsu Construction Department and the Anhui Beijing-Wu West Section Long-Distance Bus Company on joint transportation measures, and a contract will be signed soon.

The China Merchants Bureau's Hai Rui Steamer Safely Arrives at Laoyao Yesterday Afternoon

Delayed Due to Anchoring in Fog

The state-run China Merchants Bureau's Hai Rui steamer, which departed from Shanghai on the 17th of this month for the Laoyao Wharf in Haizhou to load cargo for the Longhai Railway intermodal transport, was scheduled to arrive at Laoyao on the 19th. Ministry of Railways Cancels Special Price for China Cement Company

Regarding the transportation of cement by the Longtan China Cement Company, the Jinghu and Huhangyong Railway Bureaus previously submitted a request to the Ministry of Railways to reduce the ordinary freight rate by 10% starting from September 15th of the 22nd year [of the Republic], for a period of three months. Subsequently, after the expiration of the period, because no order from the Ministry of Railways was received to continue the extension, the bureau's Transportation Department specifically issued a telegram on January 6th, numbered GB344, ordering all stations to temporarily continue the practice. At the same time, the bureau requested instructions from the Ministry of Railways. Subsequently, Instruction No. 20337 was received, stating that the price reduction for the cement should not be continued, etc. The Transportation Department was immediately instructed to cancel the special price from January 7th.

A Total of 121 People in 68 Poor Households

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau believes that every winter, charitable organizations jointly provide winter relief to poor residents of civilian residences. "According to this, this bureau has learned that every winter, your organization provides winter relief to the poor people of this place, which is of great benefit to the poor people.
